text:
This is a favorite for the kids from Hawaii. However, we don't bar-b-que it. We do basically everything you say but we put a bag of frozen chicken thighs in a big pot, bring it to a boil and let it simmer for an hour or so (the longer the better. We then serve it over rice. It's one of those meals you can make when you forget to defrost something... dinner in an hour!

text:
OMG.  Wow.  I made the Shoyu Chicken using chicken legs and served it as one of the main dishes for a family/friends cookout.  I personally don't care for chicken legs, but they seemed like the perfect food for a cookout for a large crowd.   I was so sorry that they were eaten up so quickly!  I marinated the chicken legs overnight in a ziplock bag, then grilled them slowly over a gas grill.  Meanwhile, I boiled the marinade for about 10 minutes and added just a touch of corn starch.  When the legs were about done, I brushed them with the marinade and heated through.  I can't believe how great they were.

I would give this 5 stars, but I did not grill it, because it starting pouring rain when I was going out to get the grill ready. So instead I placed the Chicken and the Marinade in a 9x13 baking dish, and baked it for 45 minutes at 400 degrees. I liked it, it was a little spicey for me, but my older boys loved it and thought it was not too spicey. I am going to be making this again when our weather here decides to stay a sunny.

text:
I'd give this 6 stars if possible!  Fabulous bbq chicken recipe worth  making over and over again.  I marinated 5 skinless, bone-in chicken thighs for 18 hours in the sauce (proportioned to 6 servings) in a ziploc bag, making sure to turn over halfway through so the meat was thoroughly marinated.  Grilled on low-medium heat for about 15 minutes per side, and served with veggie fried rice and a spinach sidedish.  While making the sides, I reduced the reserve marinade over the stovetop for about 20 minutes.  It made a super yummy sauce which was fantastic with the rest of the meal!  To sum up, the chicken turned out beautifully -- moist and flavourful with nice grill marks.  Even though it was not spicy at all, we still think it turned out perfectly.  :)

text:
Oo, so good! When I saw the picture, I had to try it. These are ingredients that are always in my house, but I never would have put them together. I'm so glad I did! Only change I made was the use of ground ginger (because that's what I had).  I cut back on the cayenne pepper just a bit because I'm a wimp when it comes to spice, but this just had a slight bite. Next time, I will let this marinate over night. One hour was good, so more must be better. We did this over low heat on the grill, about 25 minutes on each side. It was super moist. I think this marinade would be GREAT on ribs. Next time, we will probably throw this on the smoker and let it cook all day.Think it would be great served with grilled pineapple. Thanks!
Edit: We marinated ribs in this for several hours and then smoked it. Absolutely great flavor, but if you're going to use it for ribs, I would suggest doubling the brown sugar. 
Do yourself a favor, make this recipe! We made a huge batch for a BBQ and everyone couldn't stop talking about it!

I used low sodium soy sauce, used half pineapple juice/half low sodium chicken broth instead of water (for more flavor and oomph), increased the garlic and used a whole package of green onions (recipe didn't specify which kind of onions, so I just went with what sounded good). This marinated most of the night and almost all day in this wonderful, fragrant sauce and it's in the oven now, making my house smell AH-MAZING. I'll update my review once we've had a chance to taste it. EDITED: Good but quite salty, even with the reduced salt soy sauce. I didn't like the oregano in the chicken, next time I might try something else. Maybe cilantro.

Fantastic and easy, made with a lot of staples, so it was quick to pull together. Make a little extra marinade to set aside before marinating the chicken. Use this extra, boil about 10 minutes, turn off heat. Stir in one tbsp. peanut butter and whisk until smooth. Pour sauce over unseasoned ramen noodles. Makes a great base for the chicken. I also added carrots and green onions to the noodles.

text:
This not Shoyu Chicken.  It is what people in Hawaii make as Teriyaki Chicken.  I should know I am from Kaimuki on Oahu.  Shoyu Chicken is chicken braised in a sauce like teriyaki but milder because of the chicken broth you add to it.  It is cooked on the stove and simmered until done. You can add green onions also.  Real shoyu Chicken is onolisious!

text:
This is super good. I actually make this about every other week. We like spicy and so for us adding the optional spices give it the perfect hint of heat. I make the sauce as described, except I never add the oregano and I use ground ginger (instead of fresh) and green onion (instead of a normal onion), and will marinate 4 large chicken breast in the sauce for 12-24hrs. I put the chicken breasts on the grill and then boil down the left over sauce on the stove with 1 tbsp cornstarch to thicken it up. Then when its time to flip the chicken over, I will brush the top with the nice thick sauce. Cook a little longer and then flip one more time and brush that side with the thick sauce. Then I add a pinapple ring on top. and cook until done. Super yummy! We serve with white rice.

text:
This was REALLY good; might just be my new favorite way to eat grilled chicken! I didn't use cayenne pepper or red pepper flakes, but I did use about a teaspoon of McCormick's hot shot pepper blend in addition to the black pepper and that gave it just the right kick without overpowering anything. I used boneless/skinless chicken breasts instead of thighs and I also boiled down and strained the marinade to make a great sauce. It was great without the sauce, but I'd definitely recommend making the sauce for anyone trying this recipe.

text:
My husband and I made this recipe with the following exceptions: left out the oregano (it did not seem to mesh well with the other flavors to us), halved the cayenne (this gave it just a slight kick) & left out the red pepper flakes because we were out, substituted 1/2 cup pineapple juice & 1/2 cup chicken broth for water, upped the garlic to about 6-8 cloves (hard to tell because we used minced garlic), and let the thighs marinate for about 6 hours, then grilled. We also cooked the leftover marinade to reduce it and thickened with a bit of corn starch.  All these were suggestions made by other reviewers. We cut up the chicken when done put it over white rice and then poured a bit of the sauce over it.  OMG! was this ever good!! It may not be true blue Shoyu Chicken according to some, but you know what?  Whatever it is, it is well worth the time and effort!!  We had leftovers the next night and could not wait for dinner!! This stuff is good over rice, with pasta, in rollups, even sandwiches!! Do your taste buds a favor and try it, especially if you can grill it.  Happy Eating!!

text:
Fan-tastic! Really reminded me of Maui.
I've made this recipe twice now - first time with all of the optional ingredients and the second time significantly reduced. I broiled my breasts, boiled my marinade, and served with short grain (sticky) rice for true authenticity.
My advice:
1) cut the spices in half the first time you make it. They really add a KICK I wasn't expecting. You can always adjust the spiciness later because you will...
2) Boil your marinade for 10 minutes while the chicken is cooking. This gives you a wonderful, slightly reduced BBQ sauce that you can serve with the chicken. Add corn starch carefully to adjust thickness.
I will be making this recipe over and over again!

text:
I grew up in Makaha, HI, I have ate this on many occasions to say the least. Another way you can make this is by using the same ingredients as listed above. However; use 3 bottles of soy sauce (DO NOT use Kikkoman)Your first choice should be "Aloha Shoyu Sauce" and your second should be LaChoy, NEVER Kikkoman. Pour your soy sauce in a large pot and add all ingredients (including chicken).  Add enough water to make sure all chicken can be covered (probably around 5 cups or so). Bring to a boil, then simmer for 2.5 hours (3 hours if you want the chicken falling off the bone).  Serve over sticky white rice and add some of the soy sauce mixture for added flavor. You can play with the Hot spices and brown sugar to your liking. I usually add about 3 cups brown sugar and 1/4 of the red pepper and cayenne measurements, it will still be plenty spicy.

I made this recipe for dinner tonight and it was very good.  I used chicken breasts instead of thighs and marinated the chicken all afternoon (5 hours) in a zip-top bag in the fridge.  I used the food processor to blend all the marinade ingredients together.  While my husband was grilling the chicken I put the marinade in a saucepan and brought it to a boil, then thickened it with cornstarch and let it simmer to thicken (as another reviewer suggested) just before serving the chicken I spooned the sauce over.  It was great!  The reason I gave this recipe 4 stars and not 5 is that without the extra sauce upon serving the chicken would not have been very flavorful.

text:
I thought this was REALLY good, I give it 4.5 stars.  BF thought it was ok and gives it 3 stars (little too spicy for him).  I used boneless chicken breasts - was out of thighs but this sounded so good that I wanted to try it anyway.  I made half the recipe and then also used lesser amounts of the optional spices (1/3t red pepper flakes, 1/8t cayenne, 1/3t paprika).  Oh, I also reduced the black pepper because I knew that the amount called for was going to be too much for us.  Cut the chicken breasts in half, used half of the marinade on the meat for about 5 hours, reserved the other half.  Later, seared the meat on both sides using my grill pan (too hot outside today to grill); then reduced temp to low, covered, and cooked for about 15 mins.  Looked beautiful while cooking.  Meanwhile, simmered/reduced reserved marinade in saucepan, then added 1T of cornstarch dissolved in 1T of cold water to thicken.  Basted the chicken pieces on each side near the end of cooking.  Served over white rice, drizzled just a little of the basting sauce on top (don't spoon on too much, very flavorful sauce).  I thought the heat was perfect, great meal!!  Definitely making again!

We tried this last evening for the first time, and my husband cannot stop raving how fantastic these thighs are! This is a KEEPER!! And so easy. text:
Since I don't have a BBQ and fantasized about this recipe for a while I decided to use a pan to cook the chicken. I marinated the chicken with all the ingredients mentioned above except the onions and garlics, and I reduced the amount of brown sugar to no more than half a cup ( this depends on how sweet you prefer it to be). I let the chicken marinated for about an hour ( but i'm sure if I let it marinated longer it would be even better). In the pan, I first fried the onions and garlic, then added the marinated chicken and sauce. I let it cook slowly first covered for about 20 minutes then uncovered to let majority of the juice evaporate on med-low heat while flipping the chicken every 5 minutes and covering the chicken with sauce every now and then to make sure they remain moist and flavorful. The chicken came out PERFECT! It was a real REGAL! My husband licked his fingers. Definitely recommend trying it out.

text:
The first time I made this, I followed the recipe exactly and it was pretty good. However, there are a few things I do differently now to make it more like the local shoyu chicken (I live in Hawaii). I omit the oregano, (or at least tone it down) Oregano does not seem to mix with the teri style taste. Also, I slow cook the chicken in the oven for at least an hour. It lets the meat absorb the flavor and makes it really soft and tender. Shoyu chicken is supposed to be slow cooked and not grilled. With the changes, my boyfriend says this chicken is "so ono!" Thank you for a great recipe.

text:
I make this once a week. Its budget- friendly, DELICIOUS and it makes the house smell so good!! My boyfriend whose Grandma is a real hawaiian.. LOVES it!!! He says its exactly how his grandma's chicken use to taste like..I dont marinate it or grill it. I took  lisa thelen advice and I just put all the ingredients into a big pot and throw the chicken in without defrosting. Let it come to a boil and then I just simmer it and let it  cook in its sweet juices for 1 hour or until me and my man are ready to eat(the longer it simmers the better).  I serve it with rice.. winning combo! Also, sometimes I don't have chicken thighs So I just throw whats ever in the freezer..drumsticks,wings,breast and it comes out delicious still.. and if you're in a pinch ginger seasoning will do.. This recipe will be with me and my family for YEARS!!!

Awesome recipe! I skinned the chicken thighs,  marinated them or 4 hours,  baked them in the oven on 400 degrees for 20 minutes, then finished them on the grill. I boiled the marinade, as suggested by others. I used half the marinade to baste the chicken & the other half as a sauce for the stir fried snow peas I served on the side. I can't wait to make this again. Thanks!

I marinated them overnight (in separate gallon- and quart-sized bags), included all the "optional" ingredients, and got rave reviews! text:
This has been one of my family favorite for years.  I have just a couple of things I do differently. I use a 1/2 cup each brown sugar and pineapple juice and reduce the water to 1/2 cup. I also use green onion, and have never added oregano, or paprika. We usually get enough heat from the crushed red pepper and haven't had a need for the cayenne either. Everyone raves and wants the recipe. Enjoy!

text:
Fantastic! My husband doesn't like Chinese food, but he loved this chicken.
- Omitted the oregano and red pepper flakes. Any more "spicy" would have been too much.
- Used 2 Tbs powdered garlic
- Marinated a pre-cut whole fryer chicken, about 3.5 lbs., for about 2 hours.
- Baked on 400 for 20 minutes and then 375 for 40 minutes. 
- Reduced leftover sauce to BBQ consistency. 
- When chicken had about 10 minutes left, I applied thickened Shoyu sauce.
- Served with rice and pineapple. 

Hubby gave it a big "thumbs up" and said the recipe is a keeper! He even took the leftover as a chicken sandwich for lunch today. :)

We really enjoyed this.  We don't care for chicken thighs very much, so I used boneless, skinless chicken breasts instead.  Because some of the reviewers mentioned that this was pretty spicy, I omitted the red pepper flakes and reduced the amount of black pepper.  I did add about 1/4 teaspoon of cayenne pepper for a little heat.  I also didn't have any fresh ginger root, so I used about a teaspoon of ground ginger.  With these modified measurements, the flavor was fantastic without the heat being overpowering.  I also want to try this marinade on salmon sometime!

Awesome!!!  I made with chicken breasts in the slow cooker, I also marinated overnight in fridge.  After cooking in the slow cooker for about 6 hours I shredded the chicken and served over steamed rice with veggies.  I reserved some sauce to thicken and drizzle over the top.  Because I was serving to kids I used 1/2 teaspoon cayenne pepper, 1 teaspoon of red pepper flakes and no paprika.  The kids and I thought it was great, my spice loving husband wanted more kick.  So, next time I will add the spice in a portion of the sauce I thicken for him.  :)  I marinated with 12 breasts and cooked four.  We had plenty for lunch the next day and I froze the rest in baggies to use later. Thank goodness we liked it!  And I can't wait to share with all my family and friends this summer!

Amazing!  Marinated for 48 hours in everything except the cayenne pepper and the onion (I subbed in dried onion flakes as I has no onions on hand), and cooked in the oven for 40 mins @ 350F.  It is DEFINITELY a spicy dish!  My other half insisted on making another serving of the marinade to use as a sauce - not a bad idea, though our mouths were on fire for a while!  Next time, will just serve the chicken as is, with no extra marinade, to keep the spiciness down a bit :)  Excellent recipe, definitely a keeper!

text:
Made the marinade as directed (used paprika, but did not use cayenne or red pepper), but did not marinate or grill the chicken. Instead, i poured the marinade into a medium pot with four chicken thighs (the marinade was just enough to cover the four thighs), brought to a boil, and then simmered for 45 minutes or so. The results are fall-off-the-bone chicken in a delicious sauce that's awesome over rice!

We loved it! I couldn't grill it so I baked it in the oven @ 400 for an hour. I used a whole cut up chicken with no skin and left a little marinade in the bottom to baste chicken as it cooked. city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Used 4 large chicken breasts and cut recipe in half. Used ground ginger since I didn't have fresh. I did include the red pepper flakes and paprika but didn't have the cayenne. I added all the ingredients into a large gallon size ziploc baggie sealed it, and squished to mix. Then added the 4 breasts, sealed it, laid it flat so breasts didn't overlap on cookie tray, and put it in fridge. After 2 hrs I flipped bag over and let set 2 more hours. Grilled breasts on stove top grill about 10 minutes each side and boiled leftover marinade for at least 10 minutes. Then added about 2 tbsp corn bread mix (didn't have corn starch) to thicken it up.  Plated it up on white rice and spooned sauce marinade over the top of the chicken. Added a side of grilled bell pepper to complete the dinner.  Very tasty with a little kick to it.  My husband loved it and the bell pepper seemed the perfect veggie to go with it.  Leftovers heated up well the next day but seemed to have gotten spicier.

text:
i'm not from hawaii so i don't know what 'real' shoyu chicken tastes like, but this came out REALLY tender and flavorful!! it's rare that i get these recipes right on the first try which is why i have to give this five stars. i left out the ginger root, red pepper flakes, and paprika since i didn't have any at home, but it still tasted good. the cayenne pepper really gave it a kick. i think if i added the red pepper flakes it would've been way too spicy for me.

i also decided to marinate this overnight, and i believe that's the best way to do it because the flavor really soaked itself into the chicken. since i don't have a grill, i followed another reviewer's suggestion and cooked it in a big pot for 45 min - simmered it on medium/low. i also used low sodium chicken stock instead of water. i also cut down on the soy sauce b/c i thought it would be way too salty, and it still came out perfect. i will def be making this again! so fast and easy!

I made this last night. I gave it 5 stars because my husband loved it. I personally did not. But that was just a matter of personal taste. I thought that the ingredients' flavors very nicely complimented each other, though. I followed the recipe to a t, pairing it down for 8 servings. There are two things to keep in mind when reading my review.

1) I'm a foodie. I can decypher taste, smell, texture, etc.
=but=
2) It takes a lot out of me to want to cook. I'd rather my meals prepared for me by a chef, or alternative.

With that out of the way; THIS DISH IS SO EASY TO MAKE AND IS SOOO GOOD, OMG! It instantly became a fan favorite and I've made it twice already.

I baked it in the oven, separated the chicken skin/fat, and then broiled it to crisp, Pro-tip; service with coconut rice and buttered carrots.

BOOM! First review on here ;)

text:
We enjoyed this a lot! I've made it a few times now and it's been a hit every time. Plus, I usually really dislike leftover chicken, but this one works great for lunches the next day. My only tweak was to use Coconut Aminos instead of soy, due to an allergy. Coconut Aminos taste just like soy but with less sodium. I also baked the chicken in the marinade and then finished them on the grill. By baking the marinade with the chicken, it was safe to use as a sauce. I separated the onion s and solid bits from the juice, added corn starch and honey to what was left and had a great "teryaki" type sauce for spooning over the finished product. Delicious!

Yummy! I made a few changes. I used almost 3 1/2 lbs of chicken, so I had to half all the ingredients. I didn't have ginger root, so I used ground ginger instead.  After marinating the thighs in the fridge for 24 hours, I put them and all of the marinade in a 9x13 casserole pan. I did not cover them. The thighs were done in 45 minutes at 375. I poured these bad boys and the marinade over white rice and called it a day. My boys loved it. My son, who loves spicy food, said to add more spices next time. text:
I used thin chicken breasts and marinated for 2 hours adding additional spices.  I went by what was recommended in the reviews and substituted 3/4 cup chicken broth and a 1/4 cup pineapple juice. I also left out the oregano since I decided to go full on pineapple.  I baked in the oven with fresh chopped pineapple. For a side veggie I sauted a red, orange, and yellow bell pepper, along with pineapple and onion and served over steamed brown rice.  I also boiled down the marinade for a sweet sauce to baste/add for extra flavor. Prep and cook time was a bit long, but was well worth the trouble. Hubby actually took left overs to work. Yay!!!

I don't care what it's called, it was good! I made it exactly as written but will modify it a bit the next time. I also did not care for the oregano flavor and agree with another reviewer that cilantro would be complimentary. I only had time to marinate for an hour but will plan ahead next time and marinate overnight since it was not as flavorful as I was hoping. text:
Huge hit!  All three kids, ages 3-10, cleaned their plates.  I used skin on thighs because that's what I had and marinated all day in the fridge.  I put a little oriental twist to the marinade by not using oregano, substituting 1-2 T chili garlic for the assorted peppers, 1 t sesame oil, and 1/4 c rice wine vinegar.  I held back 1cup of the marinade and simmered it for a few minutes just before I served to top the chicken which I served on rice.  I cooked this on the grill on an indirect heat.  The soy and brown sugar in the marinade gave the chicken a great color and a little caramelization on the skin.  This will definitely go into our quick and easy dinner rotation.

text:
This is my go-to dinner when I need something fast, easy, and tasty! I have all the ingredients on hand, and I can use this recipe with frozen chicken for those days I forget to set meat out to defrost! You can use this recipe as a marinade for bbq chicken, but I usually make it on the stove top.  Place ingredients & chicken into a pot and bring to a boil, then simmer for 45min- 1 hour (or longer). Living in Hawaii, this is how I am used to it being served. I actually double the amount of sauce so we have enough to serve over rice.

text:
I made this for our dinner group. I used some thighs and some breasts, only because the store didn't have enough thighs that day.  Everyone said it was great. I thought the thighs were best,  maybe they soak up the marinade better. Took advice to use pineapple juice instead of the water. Definitely use some of the marinade to baste while grilling, and hold back some marinade mixture for a sauce! I boiled down marinade for 10 minutes and then added 1 tablespoon cornstarch mixed with a little water, cooking until thickened. Spooned that over the chicken, then garnished with pineapple slices and chopped green onion. Great as leftovers, too.  8/2015 update- tried this with boneless pork chops, was excellent!

text:
Fantastic all-around recipe, although personally grilling it came out relatively plain. The sauce, despite marinating for around 6 hours and 30 minutes, did not flavor the chicken thoroughly. Even if this was due to bad marination tactics, no way would grilling it be able to make the chicken as shown in the picture. The sauce is too watery, and won't stick to the chicken as the picture suggests. My second batch I made in the oven at around 350 degrees, and cooked it until it seemed done (Around 40 minutes for me). I simply put the chicken and marinade in a casserole dish and cooked it, soaking. This turned out much more flavorful and saucy, albeit softer.

I think it needs half or only 1/3 the amount of black pepper (for toddlers, SERIOUSLY take down the black pepper otherwise they will think it's too spicy), 3/4 or less of the brown sugar (and a little less ginger because I'm not a fan) but this was so delicious following the recipe exactly otherwise.  Marinated overnight - the chicken was stained beautifully the next day so clearly the marinade took!  Don't throw away that delicious marinade! Strained the leftover marinade and pulled out the onions; cooked it down with the onions to make a sauce. Served it with steamed broccoli (steamed then caramelized in a few spoonfuls of the marinade), and brown rice with a bit of the sauce. It was a PERFECT meal. If I wasn't already married, I would have been proposed to after this meal (he's still talking about it)...

I only had 4 fairly large chicken thighs (2 lbs) so I cut the marinade in half.  I let them marinade all day. Not sure what the onion added but these were absolutely delicious.  Granddaughter and I cooked them on the gas grill.  They were delicious.  They do have a little "kick" so if you don't like spicy, leave out the red pepper.  I think next time I'll use pineapple juice in place of the water.  I will cook these many more times.  UPDATE:  I have made this recipe over and over. The biggest challenge is planning ahead for the time to marinade.  Last few times I mince the onion instead of chopping and that seems to work better.  I also add a little more fresh ginger. This is one of my favorite chicken recipes.

text:
I love this recipe! I have made a similar version (without a true recipe) for years, but have used it as the sauce for a stir fry, which pairs well with either chicken or beef. People often ask how I make it and are surprised at its simplicity. I do, however, make two slight changes so that family members who must limit their intake of sugar/sodium can enjoy the recipe as well. First, I use low sodium soy sauce and, second, I substitute Cary's Sugar Free Syrup (to desired sweetness) in place of the brown sugar. (Cary's Sugar Free Syrup can be found in the pancake syrup section of the supermarket.) Even with these modifications, the recipe turns out delicious!!

text:
Definitely a keeper! Marinated 4 leg quarters for 16 hours. Boiled down the marinade and used it to baste. Started this on the grill - 15 minutes, then flipped them and cooked 10 more minutes. The wind came up, so I transferred them to a 350 F oven for another 20 minutes, covered with foil.
The only changes I made were to cut the cayenne and red pepper flakes down to 1/4 tsp. each, and I used ginger paste and garlic paste.
I saved the marinade and will try it on boneless, skinless chicken breasts in a few days.
We loved this recipe and we say "thanks" to Big E for sharing!

text:
Made this for dinner tonight with a few minor variations since I live in an apartment in Peru. 

Like many others, I baked it, and made a reduction sauce from the leftover marinade which I spread over the chicken before serving. I used ground ginger instead of fresh grated, and I used plain white sugar instead of brown because brown sugar is difficult to come by down here. Used boneless chicken breasts cut into strips, skipped the oregano, and served over vegetable fried rice. It was delicious. A very nice hint of spice but not overwhelming. I'm sure it would be even better cooked on a grill! Will be adding this one to the recipe book and making it again.
